## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on current population through density-dependent feedback mechanisms, and may include time-dependent environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-dependent rate)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic growth with periodic environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with saturating reproduction minus mortality)
- Linear density dependence with time: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (logistic with time-varying intrinsic rate)
- Hassell-type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 - c3 * P (overcompensatory density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Multiplicative P factor: dP/dt is typically proportional to P (per-capita processes), so P should appear as a multiplicative factor in most terms
- Density-dependent correction: subtraction of a term proportional to P^2 (as in c0*P - c1*P^2) indicates intraspecific competition or resource limitation
- Logarithmic density feedback: log(P) terms indicate Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate decreases logarithmically rather than linearly with density
- Ratio of polynomials in P: rational functions like P/(1+c*P) represent saturating functional responses (Type II) in reproduction or resource uptake
- Cubic terms in P (P*(P-a)*(K-P)): indicate strong Allee effects where growth is negative below a critical population threshold
- Trigonometric functions of time: sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) multiplied by growth terms capture seasonal or periodic environmental fluctuations
- Fractional powers of P: terms like P^(2/3) or P^(3/4) often arise from metabolic scaling or surface-to-volume ratio constraints in biological systems
- Additive constant term independent of P: represents immigration or stocking (constant influx regardless of population size)
- Exponential decay in time multiplied by growth: exp(-c*t) * f(P) captures resource depletion or habitat degradation over time
